    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <span id="freeText11336027713505783103" style="display:none"><b>Wunder is gathering in Nevermoor ...</b><br /><br />Morrigan Crow may have defeated her deadly curse, passed the dangerous trials and joined the mystical Wundrous Society, but her journey into Nevermoor and all its secrets has only just begun. And she is fast learning that not all magic is used for good.<br /><br />Morrigan Crow has been invited to join the prestigious Wundrous Society, a place that promised her friendship, protection and belonging for life. She's hoping for an education full of wunder, imagination and discovery - but all the Society want to teach her is how evil Wundersmiths are. And someone is blackmailing Morrigan's unit, turning her last few loyal friends against her. Has Morrigan escaped from being the cursed child of Wintersea only to become the most hated figure in Nevermoor? <br /><br />Worst of all, people have started to go missing. The fantastical city of Nevermoor, once a place of magic and safety, is now riddled with fear and suspicion...</span>

<div id="review_2590725441" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2590725441" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2590725441?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781510104440" href="/book/show/37797920-wundersmith">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2590725441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11124622974090193042">Wow, this was brilliant fun and in my opinion even better than the first in the series. I think this one gave me all those nostalgic feelings of when I first read Harry Potter, and I couldn't help but to fall in love with the world once again and get emotionally invested in the characters. There was so much to like in this book, and Morrigan's story felt a bit darker and the stakes were higher too. I think if you like the first you will love the second!<br/><br/>This book continues where the first one lea</span>
  <span id="freeText11124622974090193042" style="display:none">Wow, this was brilliant fun and in my opinion even better than the first in the series. I think this one gave me all those nostalgic feelings of when I first read Harry Potter, and I couldn't help but to fall in love with the world once again and get emotionally invested in the characters. There was so much to like in this book, and Morrigan's story felt a bit darker and the stakes were higher too. I think if you like the first you will love the second!<br /><br />This book continues where the first one leaves off. After some troublesome trials in book 1 we know that many of the students were dropped without a chance of making it to the Wonderous Society, but now it is time for the ones who have made it to go to WunSoc and learn about just what they can do. <br /><br />Morrigan is still very much unsure about her Knack and what she needs to learn about it as time goes on, but she quickly realises that although there are some firm friends who support her, she needs to earn the loyalty of those others in her group. She is forced to attend some mind-numbingly boring classes and yet she is also expected to keep her magic under wraps, and she has to do all of this whilst her guardian is once more absent for most of the book. Also, there's a whole lot of people disappearing strangely and she is more than likely going to get mixed up in the trouble because trouble just seems to find her...<br /><br />What I loved about this was seeing the streets that changed as you went down them and the markets which were filled with magic and mayhem. There are seasonal celebrations, festivals, dramatic events and wondrous surprises that Morrigan can barely believe. Nevermoor has so many secrets to offer if you can just start to understand it and believe in it, and this is the real beginning of Morrigan's time to explore. <br /><br />Overall, the plot and the magic were great and the characters became even better in this one too. I thoroughly enjoyed this and read it all in two sittings, and I highly recommend this as one to just lose yourself in for an evening. The magic will give you Harry Potter nostalgia, but the story is unique and wonderful too. 5*s from me :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11124622974090193042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49847688-emily?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2705167026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13370420552138875038">What can I say except I LOVE THIS SERIES.<br/><br/>Once again, Townsend pulls you into a world of wunder and whimsy, and doesn't let go. We follow Morrigan as she begins classes as the Wundrous Society, and follow her on a journey about belonging and finding yourself.<br/><br/>Like many of the great classics of children's literature, Townsend plays with the fallibility of adults. What do you do when the people who are <i>supposed</i> to look out for you, to know what to do when faced with challenges, aren't there to help?</span>
  <span id="freeText13370420552138875038" style="display:none">What can I say except I LOVE THIS SERIES.<br /><br />Once again, Townsend pulls you into a world of wunder and whimsy, and doesn't let go. We follow Morrigan as she begins classes as the Wundrous Society, and follow her on a journey about belonging and finding yourself.<br /><br />Like many of the great classics of children's literature, Townsend plays with the fallibility of adults. What do you do when the people who are <i>supposed</i> to look out for you, to know what to do when faced with challenges, aren't there to help? What do you do when well-meaning adults make choices that ultimately harm you or your friends? What do you do when those with power actively wield that power in harmful ways? Townsend explores these questions with care and nuance.<br /><br />I love that in a book about inclusivity and belonging, Townsend has clearly taken the time to craft a world that is itself inclusive. We see a diverse range of characters, and that diversity never feels shoehorned in. We also don't get any of that, "Well, I never said Hermione <i>wasn't</i> Black!" retcon nonsense--characters of color are described as such, made plain in the text. All children deserve to feel seen in the stories they consume, and it's lovely to see a book that puts in the effort to include representation.<br /><br />As a sequel, this is fantastic. The world is expanded, the stakes are raised, and it has a distinctly darker tone than the first book. The well-meaning adults feel more insidious, the villain is more villainous. <br /><br />I can't wait for this serious to continue.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13370420552138875038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Morrigan was thrilled to finally have a family; to have people who cared about her.   <span id="freeText5197356156790587106" style="display:none">Nine young people in Morrigan Crow’s unit – nine who had said under oath to be friends, be loyal to each other. Morrigan was thrilled to finally have a family; to have people who cared about her. When they all began their classes, the students had ingenious and exciting things to learn – all except Morrigan, whose teacher would concentrate on Wundersmith’s alone – and how evil and degraded they all were, both past and present. Morrigan’s patron, Jupiter North, did all he could to change the Elder’s minds about her classes, but they wouldn’t be budged…<br /><br />When first one, then another went missing, Jupiter was away, searching constantly. His nephew Jack was occasionally by Morrigan’s side – when his schooling allowed – as was her best friend Hawthorne. But with the blackmailing threats focused on Morrigan’s group, she feared she would have no one left by her side. Everyone blamed her for the misfortunes that were happening – what could she do? And what had Ezra Squall to do with it all? The fear rippling through Nevermoor was infiltrating everyone.<br /><br />Wow! What.A.Ride!! <i>Wundersmith</i> is the second in the Nevermoor series by Aussie author Jessica Townsend, and it is just as fantastical and exciting as the first. Fast paced with loads of action, plenty of magic and heart stopping tension, <i>Wundersmith</i> is one I highly recommend. But I also suggest <i>Nevermoor</i> be read first so the full benefit of the series is felt.<br /> <br />With thanks to Hachette AU for my ARC to read in exchange for an honest review.</span>

  <span id="freeText13095627641970805344" style="display:none">In this follow up to the highly original Nevermoor, Jessica Townsend continues the adventures of Morrigan Crow as she is admitted into the Wundrous society and sent to the Wundrous Society headquarters to receive her education along with the other successful applicants. While everyone else in her group is doing really interesting subjects, Morrigan is frustrated that the society doesn't seem to want her to learn anything useful. Jupiter is too distracted to help her as he is busy looking for a number of missing people and creatures and doesn't realise that she might be in danger. <br /><br />This is a series that will delight children and parents alike as Morrigan navigates her way through trying to do make friends, and do the right thing which sometimes means disobeying the rules and getting into dangerous situations. The characters are developing well and the stage is now set for Morrigan to develop as a Wundersmith and to have a showdown with the evil Ezra Squall.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13095627641970805344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Saying anything more about the finale of the first book or elaborating further on the title of this book, will amount to revealing spoilers for the first book.   <span id="freeText4419282246419754898" style="display:none">The adorable quirky tales of Ms. Morrigan Crow continue...and her adventures get even more exciting...<br /><br />After having barely passed her trials, Mog is left confused and bewildered. Saying anything more about the finale of the first book or elaborating further on the title of this book, will amount to revealing spoilers for the first book. So, I'll keep mum. <br /><br />This book gives more reasons to the reader to draw parallels with Harry Potter. The stand-offs with the adversary, questioning one's own goodness, and an outlandishly faithful, loyal and protective parental figure will stir all those feelings inside you.<br /><br />But, for me, I consider HP as the trope that the Nevermoor exploits and masters beautifully! <br />And the fact, that I can forget my adult problems and be a child again while in this whimsically crafted universe is a reason enough for me to read each and every book in the series that are yet to come out.<br /><br />Oh, and...<br /><br /><b>4.5 stars</b><br />:)<br />---------------------------------------------------------------------------<br />There is something so uniquely endearing about this series, that even in the middle of a horrible reading slump, I flew through this in ONE DAY...<br /><br />Full RTC.. :)</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=great-worldbuilding">great-worldbuilding</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3518261574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13785557279981703641">This series is such a breath of fresh air for the fantasy reader - if you haven't read them yet, why not? Don't let the middle grade label fool you. This story is for everyone. <br/><br/><b>World building:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Plot/Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br/><b>Enjoyment:</b> ★★★★★<br/><b>Character development:</b> ★★★★★<br/><br/><b>Morrigan Crow thought her problems were over.</b> After discovering in <i>Nevermoor: The Trials of Morrigan Crow</i> that she was NOT a cursed child in a boring world and that there was a whole new world of magical people waiting for her, Morrigan thou</span>
  <span id="freeText13785557279981703641" style="display:none">This series is such a breath of fresh air for the fantasy reader - if you haven't read them yet, why not? Don't let the middle grade label fool you. This story is for everyone. <br /><br /><b>World building:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Plot/Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br /><b>Enjoyment:</b> ★★★★★<br /><b>Character development:</b> ★★★★★<br /><br /><b>Morrigan Crow thought her problems were over.</b> After discovering in <i>Nevermoor: The Trials of Morrigan Crow</i> that she was NOT a cursed child in a boring world and that there was a whole new world of magical people waiting for her, Morrigan thought she could breathe. <br /><br />Oh dear. Not quite yet, Morrigan. <br /><br />The city of Nevermoor and the Wundrous Society of magical people might be a glittering place filled with whimsy, magic, and promise—but <b>it's also hiding quite a few secrets and prejudices.</b> Especially when it comes to Morrigan. Without getting into spoilers for the first book, let's just say that Morrigan has her own kind of magic. While powerful and life-changing, it's also something that the residents of Nevermoor appear to fear. <b>Society always fears the unknown, the uncontrollable. Nevermoor is no exception</b>. <br /><br />She should be enjoying her first year as a junior scholar to the Wundrous Society with her 8 fellow students. Instead, <b>Morrigan discovers that the mantle of "cursed" can mean many different things, and she's still an Outsider.</b> <br /><br /><b>But then the people and beings of Nevermoor begin to disappear... and Morrigan might be the only one who can connect the dots.</b> With the help of her dragon-riding friend, Hawthorne, and a series of mysterious events, she sets off to discover the truth. <br /><br /><b>It just might not be the truth she expects to find.</b> <br /><br /><u>
  <b>My thoughts:</b>
</u> <br />What a sophisticated and unexpected sophomore novel for a middle grade fantasy series?! I don't mean to put down other series or to sound condescending—<b>it's just rare to find authentic surprises when you're in a genre with established tropes. <i>Wundersmith</i> was just that: something NEW, and a surprise.</b> <br /><br />I also loved the <b>deeper emotional burdens and complex relationship dynamics</b> at play. Morrigan is not quite an "anti" Chosen One, but her experience as someone who is continually pushed to the fringes of acceptance in Nevermoor opened the door to so many different <b>conversations of Othering, fearing the "unknown" to the point of harmful labeling, and what happens when Society decides to let fear and bigotry rule</b> the conversation. <br /><br />Oh, and obviously the world building and magical setting—<b>I would live in this world in a HEARTBEAT</b>. Lovely premise, lovely cityscape, lovely magic. The best. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.amyimogenereads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/amyimogenereads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13785557279981703641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i> Date read: </i>
</b> January 4-January 7, 2019 <br /><br /><b> Actual Rating: 4.50 STARS </b><br /><br />Unsurprisingly, I loved it almost as much as the first book. Yes, almost, though not that big of a difference, really. Dropped a half star from my rating because this time, I found a little something that made me rolled my eyes out of frustration for a couple of times. And it was Morrigan's stubbornness, impulsiveness and a few times settling for some exasperating decisions. Yeah, I know she's just a child, and being a child involves being reckless. And I fully understand that, that's why I only dropped half a star because she has a solid excuse for her decisions. Because if the ways were made by some teenager or adult, oh boy! One of the things I hate is having a main character with idiotic and frustrating way of solving things.<br /><br />BUT! Other than that single complaint, everything is what I hoped for in this spectacular and magical world. I still craved for more Jupiter and Hawthorne and Jack scenes. I hope there will be more of those in the next books. I still loved this so much! And I can't wait for the next books to come out.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7030675880935622553">After the wundrously magical and funny <i>Nevermoor - The Trials of Morrigan Crow</i> our main protagonist returns picking up where we left off. Having successfully made it through the trials in book one Morrigan will join Hawthorne and seven other scholars in Unit 919 studying at the prestigious Wundrous Society. The unit will need all there knacks as they navigate their ways through a challenging 6 months.<br/><br/>Morrigan will have to fight through the stigma of being a Wundersmith in a land that fears them.</span>
  <span id="freeText7030675880935622553" style="display:none">After the wundrously magical and funny <i>Nevermoor - The Trials of Morrigan Crow</i> our main protagonist returns picking up where we left off. Having successfully made it through the trials in book one Morrigan will join Hawthorne and seven other scholars in Unit 919 studying at the prestigious Wundrous Society. The unit will need all there knacks as they navigate their ways through a challenging 6 months.<br /><br />Morrigan will have to fight through the stigma of being a Wundersmith in a land that fears them. Trying to control her abilities while learning about her kinds history is made even further complicated by one of her own who is currently banished doing everything in his power to make her, against her will, realize her full potential. <br /><br />With themes as varied as privilege, prejudice, and friendship, overall this is another fine read with one slight caveat. For me at least there was little surprise with what happens and as a result made for a less memorable experience. Don't get me wrong, the writing was again superb, and the whole idea of the Wundrous Society and Morrigan trying to comes to terms with her identity as a Wundersmith is fascinating while there was more than a hint of <i> Neil Gaiman's Coraline</i>. But when you know where things are heading from the word go, it feels more like a stepping stone for book three. </span>

    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5837456-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372225128p2/5837456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2581143326?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/5837456-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2581143326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16252431893988390890">This book follows on from, “Nevermoor: The Trials of Morrigan Crow.” We met Morrigan in the first book, where we discovered her story. Cursed, she was destined to die on her eleventh birthday; plus all of the bad luck that occurs is blamed on her. However, before her fate overtakes her, she is whisked away by a man called Jupiter North to the secret city of Nevermoor, where she is given the chance to join the Wundrous Society.<br/><br/>However, of course, despite having escaped her fate, life is not going</span>
  <span id="freeText16252431893988390890" style="display:none">This book follows on from, “Nevermoor: The Trials of Morrigan Crow.” We met Morrigan in the first book, where we discovered her story. Cursed, she was destined to die on her eleventh birthday; plus all of the bad luck that occurs is blamed on her. However, before her fate overtakes her, she is whisked away by a man called Jupiter North to the secret city of Nevermoor, where she is given the chance to join the Wundrous Society.<br /><br />However, of course, despite having escaped her fate, life is not going to be quite so easy. Morrigan is taught that all Wundersmiths are evil and that, rather than embrace her new powers, she must learn to suppress her mysterious ability. Nevermoor is turning out to be a place of danger, rather than the haven of safety, she had first thought…<br /><br />My eleven year old daughter loves this series, but, without doubt, these books are designed to appeal to adults as well as children. At just over 400 pages, this has enough depth to offer more than the average novel aimed at older children. With Morrigan’s patron, Jupiter North, away, she is, again, very much on her own and there is a real sense of danger in these pages, which will entice the reader to want to read on. Overall, this is an excellent sequel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16252431893988390890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3037408492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3037408492" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3037408492?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781510104440" href="/book/show/37797920-wundersmith">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=childrens-book">childrens-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3037408492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1966959534745653660">Magic schools and wondrous knacks make for an outstanding children's story in Jessica Townsend's follow up to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34219873.The_Trials_of_Morrigan_Crow__Nevermoor___1_' title='The Trials of Morrigan Crow (Nevermoor, #1) by Jessica Townsend' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Trials of Morrigan Crow</a>. As an illustrious new member of the Wunderous Society, Morrigan must face new challenges and new tests in her journey to uncover the mystery behind missing Arcanes, while also getting her new classmates to like her. Not such an easy task when they're terrified of your knack. <br/><br/>I loved this. Not only is it wonderfully written, filled with all the magical joy and</span>
  <span id="freeText1966959534745653660" style="display:none">Magic schools and wondrous knacks make for an outstanding children's story in Jessica Townsend's follow up to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34219873.The_Trials_of_Morrigan_Crow__Nevermoor___1_" title="The Trials of Morrigan Crow (Nevermoor, #1) by Jessica Townsend" rel="nofollow noopener">The Trials of Morrigan Crow</a>. As an illustrious new member of the Wunderous Society, Morrigan must face new challenges and new tests in her journey to uncover the mystery behind missing Arcanes, while also getting her new classmates to like her. Not such an easy task when they're terrified of your knack. <br /><br />I loved this. Not only is it wonderfully written, filled with all the magical joy and excitement I want in a children's story, but also featuring complicated and we'll developed characters. Morrigan is still struggling with who she is, and coming out of a horrible childhood where she wasn't wanted. Several times, when things go wrong, she blames herself. She's hiding herself, and this is bolstered by the WunSoc also trying to hide her away. I loved seeing her come out of this shell and discovering herself and experience life and realising she's special. I also love all of her unit. Each character has a special knack, something that makes them different and I liked exploring each of them. I particularly loved Cadence and Hawthorne and their growing friendship. No matter what Morrigan does, Hawthorne takes it in his stride and knows she's a good person. In many respects he keeps her grounded and allows her to explore herself. Cadence is the friend who will push Morrigan outside of her comfort zone, knowing she can handle it. In the background, as a constant if chaotic father figure is Jupiter North. Charismatic, ginger, good natured. He's rather wonderful. <br /><br />The story and plot are also so well done. There's a running mystery throughout involving missing people, but we also get a better look at the world of Nevermoor and all its tricks. There are strange passageways, unusual corridors and a subterranean school all waiting to be discovered. At no point did I feel the plot dragged, and I was fully invested in this world and characters. The pacing is fantastic, skipping from adventure to reveal and beyond managing to balance that fine line between action and rest without it ever feeling like a chore. <br /><br />This series just seems to get better and better, as we delve deeper into the mythology of Nevermoor and examine hints of greater machinations in the background. Morrigan has a lot on her young shoulders, and it doesn't look like it's going to let up for her any time soon. And I can't wait to see what's next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1966959534745653660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16748684770242785997"><i>
  <b>Wundersmith</b>
</i> is an exciting, greatly entertaining sequel to Nevermoor. To think that Morrigan Crow’s cursed life is behind her is a big mistake. Life at Wunsoc is not all sunshine and rainbows for Morrigan as she struggles to find her place within the prestigious Wundrous Society due to her very <i>unique</i> knack—aka being a <i>Wundersmith</i>—which is greatly feared and/or hated in Nevermoor.<br/><br/><b>Pros:</b><br/><br/>✨ I love the gradual development of Morrigan’s friendship with Cadence and the her continual friendship with</span>
  <span id="freeText16748684770242785997" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Wundersmith</b>
</i> is an exciting, greatly entertaining sequel to Nevermoor. To think that Morrigan Crow’s cursed life is behind her is a big mistake. Life at Wunsoc is not all sunshine and rainbows for Morrigan as she struggles to find her place within the prestigious Wundrous Society due to her very <i>unique</i> knack—aka being a <i>Wundersmith</i>—which is greatly feared and/or hated in Nevermoor.<br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br />✨ I love the gradual development of Morrigan’s friendship with Cadence and the her continual friendship with Hawthorne<br /><br />✨ The pacing was just great; good build up to the climax. Jessica Townsend didn’t waste time with the unnecessary details which I greatly appreciated. <br /><br />✨ I love the expansion of the Nevermoor. There is always a surprise around the corner in that city. <br /><br />✨ Squall’s character is more intriguing than meets the eye. <br /><br />✨ I love how Morrigan is slowly growing into her power despite the objections from most people in the Society.<br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br /><br />✨ In terms of my enjoyment, I was annoyed with how everyone perceived/treated Morrigan and, although it’s understandable, no child should go through all those misconceptions. Though it does speak to the talent of the writer to make me care so much for the characters, especially when they are so wholesome. <br /><br />I just absolutely love this series. I’m finally getting all the Harry Potter vibes I was looking for.</span>

<div id="review_2143675664" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143675664" />
    <a title="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd"><img alt="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479923328p2/11177071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143675664?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" href="/user/show/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd">Kelly (Diva Booknerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd?shelf=bookgasm">bookgasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd?shelf=loveozmg">loveozmg</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd?shelf=hachette">hachette</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143675664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16215527414822683193">Miss Morrigan Crow, calamitous young lady of the Wintersea Republic is now preparing to become an esteemed scholar of the Wundrous Society, accompanying eight fellow students including the marvellous Hawthorne. Although compelled to confidentiality considering the dastardly mayhem instigated by Wundersmith Ezra Squall, Morrigan's Wundersmith ability is discovered and unscrupulously, an unknown antagonist is conspiring towards the extraordinary children with a bizarre series of anonymous notes an</span>
  <span id="freeText16215527414822683193" style="display:none">Miss Morrigan Crow, calamitous young lady of the Wintersea Republic is now preparing to become an esteemed scholar of the Wundrous Society, accompanying eight fellow students including the marvellous Hawthorne. Although compelled to confidentiality considering the dastardly mayhem instigated by Wundersmith Ezra Squall, Morrigan's Wundersmith ability is discovered and unscrupulously, an unknown antagonist is conspiring towards the extraordinary children with a bizarre series of anonymous notes and peculiar stipulations.<br /><br />Fragments throughout the Wundrous Society community have vanished, scholars, colleagues and acquaintances. Instinctively Miss Morrigan Crow is a suspect as an accused nefarious Wundersmith but with the steadfast assistance of the nonchalant Hawthorne, Jupiter North, Jack and an unlikely collaborator, Morrigan is determined to preserve the Wundrous Society, Nevermoor and substantiate that a Wundersmith is fantastically wundrous.<br /><br /><b>Our Magnificent Morrigan!</b><br />Morrigan Crow is a intelligent and practical young woman. Forsaking the calamity and misadventure of the Wintersea Republic, Morrigan is now a resident of Nevermoor, liberated by Jupiter North to compete in the Wondrous Society tournament. As a Wundersmith, Morrigan attends a specialised program consisting of the history of the Wundersmith and their heinous atrocities. <br /><br />Throughout the narration, Morrigan discovers that beneath the fantastical facade of Nevermoor, wickedness is awakening. Jupiter North is investigating an illegal marketplace in correlation to the community members. His extended absences further isolating Morrigan as she adjusts to her new environment. Morrigan is challenged by prejudice and at a disadvantage, increasingly isolated from her fellow scholars and Society facility, fearing the Wundersmith notoriety. Her Society companions are disciplined within their individual abilities however, Morrigan is secluded and denied an education despite Jupiter protesting for equality. The demeanour of Wundersmith Ezra Squall reflects on Morrigan and although only twelve years of age, she is held responsible for the actions of her predecessor. Outlandish! <br /><br /><b>The Merry Band Of Sidekicks</b><br />The grand Hotel Deucalion is resident to a fictionally diverse and eclectic community and although Jupiter is her guardian, Morrigan relies upon the Deucalion residents for guidance and perspective. Fenestra the talking Magnificat, Jack the nephew of Jupiter who returns from boarding school on weekends, the operatic singer and the vampire dwarf with a penchant for lavish carousing. <br /><br />Hawthorne Swift is a tremendous character, friend and entourage for Morrigan. His solidarity is unconditional and although his character appears humorous and sprightly, he fiercely defends his friend against Morrigan naysayers. Former antagonist Cadance Blackburn is delightfully surprising. Although adversaries, Cadance recognises the importance of Morrigan and her abilities as they cooperate to solve the mystery of the illegal marketplace.<br /><br /><b>Step Boldly</b><br />The atmospheric enchantment of Nevermoor is an experience. The fantastical Brolly Rail as it bustles throughout the expansive metropolis, the intricate and deceptive thoroughfares and animated diorama of Nevermoor and the residents. Nevermoor is fantastically imagined and beautifully illustrated. Although the world is intricate and voluminous, it's encompassed by a wonderful intimacy and warmth.<br /><br />Nevermoor transcends children's literature, captivating and enchanting audiences. Categorically breathtaking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16215527414822683193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I enjoyed how Wundersmith was diff in experience. There is more wonder (and Wunder), the new kids at school get to know each other, there are blackmail secret letters, ghastly markets with all sorts dark stuff, and more. So enjoyable! Though I do wish we had more of the M</span>

<div id="review_3056332893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3056332893" />
    <a title="Mara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70492479-mara"><img alt="Mara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572141381p2/70492479.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3056332893?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/70492479-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70492479-mara?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70492479-mara?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3056332893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16285272375754048818">I finally polished this one off-- and definitely enjoyed it more than the first installment. I think thematically this book is doing interesting things, and I particularly like the themes around confronting our own inner darkness & the reality of people having both good and bad sides for a middle grade novel. This is a series that has a decidedly dark flavor to it, which I'm digging now that I'm fully into the story, and I'm excited to see where the series goes next. I was going back and forth b</span>
  <span id="freeText16285272375754048818" style="display:none">I finally polished this one off-- and definitely enjoyed it more than the first installment. I think thematically this book is doing interesting things, and I particularly like the themes around confronting our own inner darkness &amp; the reality of people having both good and bad sides for a middle grade novel. This is a series that has a decidedly dark flavor to it, which I'm digging now that I'm fully into the story, and I'm excited to see where the series goes next. I was going back and forth between the physical book &amp; the audio, but I think going forward I'm just going to commit to the audio - very much enjoy the production </span>
  <a data-text-id="16285272375754048818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2807273601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2807273601" />
    <a title="Ryan Buckby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32429909-ryan-buckby"><img alt="Ryan Buckby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528436487p2/32429909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2807273601?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Buckby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Buckby" href="/user/show/32429909-ryan-buckby">Ryan Buckby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2807273601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1079031106960726610">as far as sequels go i think i'm pretty darn happy with how this one went and that's saying a lot for me with sequels these days. <br/><br/><b> Plot: </b> picking things right up after the events of book one and Morrigan is living in Hotel Deucalion and is now in the wonder society after passing her test from the previous year. When i first started reading this book i just missed it so much and instantly jumped right back into this world that i had missed for so long between my reading it. <br/><br/>This book to me had th</span>
  <span id="freeText1079031106960726610" style="display:none">as far as sequels go i think i'm pretty darn happy with how this one went and that's saying a lot for me with sequels these days. <br /><br /><b> Plot: </b> picking things right up after the events of book one and Morrigan is living in Hotel Deucalion and is now in the wonder society after passing her test from the previous year. When i first started reading this book i just missed it so much and instantly jumped right back into this world that i had missed for so long between my reading it. <br /><br />This book to me had the feel of Harry Potter elements in it and i hate comparing books but i just got that feel from it, from the home train, to the 919 unit and the school it just all felt like that. The whole knack system is very intriguing to me because everyone is so different and not ranking from best to worst and think that having this type of system were everyone is treated equally is so much better and it works really well. <br /><br />We get to explore more of this world which i really enjoyed doing because we only really got the majority of the scenes at the hotel in book one. Going into the city more and exploring as Morrigan did was fascinating and i especially loved the market part of the book with all the different stalls and magic elements thrown in it was just pure joy that i felt like Morrigan did while being there. <br /><br /><br />Those trick things that Morrigan and her other unit 919 members went through and had to learn how to use them i found them really interesting, having something that can be anything at random until the person goes in and finds out what it is was really interesting. <br /><br /><br />Morrigan has grown so much from book one and i'm glad she has now finally accepted herself more and has less self doubt of herself in this book than she did in the pervious one. However things are also put into question for her when everyone is told of Morrigan being a wundersmith as they are considered dangerous this is kept a secret. I do love how she does not for one second let this define her not even one bit and i love how much self growth this character has done and it shows in that. <br /><br /><br />I do love the friendship between Morrigan and Hawthorne because no matter the situation these two remain close and are still there to help each other no matter what and this is what a true friendship is supposed to look like. Hawthorne has such huge loyalty to Morrigan and her as well that they can confide in each other to keep secrets and just help each other out and its one book friendship that i just love. <br /><br /><br />One thing i also liked is how there are many different bigger topics that are explained to a middle grade audience and Jessica did a really good job at writing them and explaining it in the proper way. <br /><br /><br />I really do need a third book because i don't think i'm ready for this series to end just yet and i could use some more story and this world!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1079031106960726610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WffLbTfBcgZWkC0dSKaYV1KH6Pm1o0SfrYjnPclglXDgRhQGaM75TqN1yRjN5TKSGKuJZ6DtaPRscWaRCoSoCg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PVW2dlTl+/bY1KHWeJ/Z/JomLK0S353hXPrRgf7EZD6E5GkdC+pwvi0xRdP93HM50ApNMweRsYqdA1AtPSBZRA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
